\subsection{Detailed Description}
\subsection*{Block Ciphers and Symmetric Ciphers}

This file documents the A\+PI for block ciphers and other symmetric ciphers.

\subsubsection*{Procedural A\+PI}

For a block cipher implementation, up to three separate sets of functions are provided, for C\+BC encryption, C\+BC decryption, and C\+TR encryption/decryption. Each set has its own context structure, initialised with the encryption key.

For C\+BC encryption and decryption, the data to encrypt or decrypt is referenced as a sequence of blocks. The implementations assume that there is no partial block; no padding is applied or removed. The caller is responsible for handling any kind of padding.

Function for C\+TR encryption are defined only for block ciphers with blocks of 16 bytes or more (i.\+e. A\+ES, but not D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES).

Each implemented block cipher is identified by an \char`\"{}internal name\char`\"{} from which are derived the names of structures and functions that implement the cipher. For the block cipher of internal name \char`\"{}`xxx`\char`\"{}, the following are defined\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+\+B\+L\+O\+C\+K\+\_\+\+S\+I\+ZE}

A macro that evaluates to the block size (in bytes) of the cipher. For all implemented block ciphers, this value is a power of two.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+keys}

Context structure that contains the subkeys resulting from the key expansion. These subkeys are appropriate for C\+BC encryption. The structure first field is called {\ttfamily vtable} and points to the appropriate O\+OP structure.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+init(br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, const void $\ast$key, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform key expansion\+: subkeys for C\+BC encryption are computed and written in the provided context structure. The key length M\+U\+ST be adequate for the implemented block cipher. This function also sets the {\ttfamily vtable} field.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+run(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$iv, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform C\+BC encryption of {\ttfamily len} bytes, in place. The encrypted data replaces the cleartext. {\ttfamily len} M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block length (if it is not, the function may loop forever or overflow a buffer). The IV is provided with the {\ttfamily iv} pointer; it is also updated with a copy of the last encrypted block.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+keys}

Context structure that contains the subkeys resulting from the key expansion. These subkeys are appropriate for C\+BC decryption. The structure first field is called {\ttfamily vtable} and points to the appropriate O\+OP structure.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+init(br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, const void $\ast$key, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform key expansion\+: subkeys for C\+BC decryption are computed and written in the provided context structure. The key length M\+U\+ST be adequate for the implemented block cipher. This function also sets the {\ttfamily vtable} field.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+run(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$iv, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t num\+\_\+blocks)}

Perform C\+BC decryption of {\ttfamily len} bytes, in place. The decrypted data replaces the ciphertext. {\ttfamily len} M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block length (if it is not, the function may loop forever or overflow a buffer). The IV is provided with the {\ttfamily iv} pointer; it is also updated with a copy of the last {\itshape encrypted} block.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+keys}

Context structure that contains the subkeys resulting from the key expansion. These subkeys are appropriate for C\+TR encryption and decryption. The structure first field is called {\ttfamily vtable} and points to the appropriate O\+OP structure.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+init(br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, const void $\ast$key, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform key expansion\+: subkeys for C\+TR encryption and decryption are computed and written in the provided context structure. The key length M\+U\+ST be adequate for the implemented block cipher. This function also sets the {\ttfamily vtable} field.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+run(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, const void $\ast$iv, uint32\+\_\+t cc, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)} (returns {\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t})

Perform C\+TR encryption/decryption of some data. Processing is done \char`\"{}in place\char`\"{} (the output data replaces the input data). This function implements the \char`\"{}standard incrementing function\char`\"{} from N\+I\+ST S\+P800-\/38A, annex B\+: the IV length shall be 4 bytes less than the block size (i.\+e. 12 bytes for A\+ES) and the counter is the 32-\/bit value starting with {\ttfamily cc}. The data length ({\ttfamily len}) is not necessarily a multiple of the block size. The new counter value is returned, which supports chunked processing, provided that each chunk length (except possibly the last one) is a multiple of the block size.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+keys}

Context structure that contains the subkeys resulting from the key expansion. These subkeys are appropriate for doing combined C\+TR encryption/decryption and C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC, as used in the C\+CM and E\+AX authenticated encryption modes. The structure first field is called {\ttfamily vtable} and points to the appropriate O\+OP structure.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+init(br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, const void $\ast$key, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform key expansion\+: subkeys for combined C\+TR encryption/decryption and C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC are computed and written in the provided context structure. The key length M\+U\+ST be adequate for the implemented block cipher. This function also sets the {\ttfamily vtable} field.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+encrypt(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$ctr, void $\ast$cbcmac, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform C\+TR encryption of some data, and C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC. Processing is done \char`\"{}in place\char`\"{} (the output data replaces the input data). This function applies C\+TR encryption on the data, using a full block-\/size counter (i.\+e. for 128-\/bit blocks, the counter is incremented as a 128-\/bit value). The \textquotesingle{}ctr\textquotesingle{} array contains the initial value for the counter (used in the first block) and it is updated with the new value after data processing. The \textquotesingle{}cbcmac\textquotesingle{} value shall point to a block-\/sized value which is used as IV for C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC, computed over the encrypted data (output of C\+TR encryption); the resulting C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC is written over \textquotesingle{}cbcmac\textquotesingle{} on output.

The data length M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block size.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+decrypt(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$ctr, void $\ast$cbcmac, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform C\+TR decryption of some data, and C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC. Processing is done \char`\"{}in place\char`\"{} (the output data replaces the input data). This function applies C\+TR decryption on the data, using a full block-\/size counter (i.\+e. for 128-\/bit blocks, the counter is incremented as a 128-\/bit value). The \textquotesingle{}ctr\textquotesingle{} array contains the initial value for the counter (used in the first block) and it is updated with the new value after data processing. The \textquotesingle{}cbcmac\textquotesingle{} value shall point to a block-\/sized value which is used as IV for C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC, computed over the encrypted data (input of C\+TR encryption); the resulting C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC is written over \textquotesingle{}cbcmac\textquotesingle{} on output.

The data length M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block size.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+ctr(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$ctr, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}

Perform C\+TR encryption or decryption of the provided data. The data is processed \char`\"{}in place\char`\"{} (the output data replaces the input data). A full block-\/sized counter is applied (i.\+e. for 128-\/bit blocks, the counter is incremented as a 128-\/bit value). The \textquotesingle{}ctr\textquotesingle{} array contains the initial value for the counter (used in the first block), and it is updated with the new value after data processing.

The data length M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block size.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+mac(const br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+keys $\ast$ctx, void $\ast$cbcmac, const void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}

Compute C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC over the provided data. The IV for C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC is provided as \textquotesingle{}cbcmac\textquotesingle{}; the output is written over the same array. The data itself is untouched. The data length M\+U\+ST be a multiple of the block size.
\end{DoxyItemize}

It shall be noted that the key expansion functions return {\ttfamily void}. If the provided key length is not allowed, then there will be no error reporting; implementations need not validate the key length, thus an invalid key length may result in undefined behaviour (e.\+g. buffer overflow).

Subkey structures contain no interior pointer, and no external resources are allocated upon key expansion. They can thus be discarded without any explicit deallocation.

\subsubsection*{Object-\/\+Oriented A\+PI}

Each context structure begins with a field (called {\ttfamily vtable}) that points to an instance of a structure that references the relevant functions through pointers. Each such structure contains the following\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily context\+\_\+size}

The size (in bytes) of the context structure for subkeys.
\item {\ttfamily block\+\_\+size}

The cipher block size (in bytes).
\item {\ttfamily log\+\_\+block\+\_\+size}

The base-\/2 logarithm of cipher block size (e.\+g. 4 for blocks of 16 bytes).
\item {\ttfamily init}

Pointer to the key expansion function.
\item {\ttfamily run}

Pointer to the encryption/decryption function.
\end{DoxyItemize}

For combined C\+T\+R/\+C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC encryption, the {\ttfamily vtable} has a slightly different structure\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily context\+\_\+size}

The size (in bytes) of the context structure for subkeys.
\item {\ttfamily block\+\_\+size}

The cipher block size (in bytes).
\item {\ttfamily log\+\_\+block\+\_\+size}

The base-\/2 logarithm of cipher block size (e.\+g. 4 for blocks of 16 bytes).
\item {\ttfamily init}

Pointer to the key expansion function.
\item {\ttfamily encrypt}

Pointer to the C\+TR encryption + C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC function.
\item {\ttfamily decrypt}

Pointer to the C\+TR decryption + C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC function.
\item {\ttfamily ctr}

Pointer to the C\+TR encryption/decryption function.
\item {\ttfamily mac}

Pointer to the C\+B\+C-\/\+M\+AC function.
\end{DoxyItemize}

For block cipher \char`\"{}`xxx`\char`\"{}, static, constant instances of these structures are defined, under the names\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+vtable}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+vtable}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+vtable}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+xxx\+\_\+ctrcbc\+\_\+vtable}
\end{DoxyItemize}

\subsubsection*{Implemented Block Ciphers}

Provided implementations are\+:

\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu} spread 0pt [c]{*{4}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\rowcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Name }&\textbf{ Function }&\PBS\centering \textbf{ Block Size (bytes) }&\PBS\centering \textbf{ Key lengths (bytes)  }\\\cline{1-4}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\rowcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ Name }&\textbf{ Function }&\PBS\centering \textbf{ Block Size (bytes) }&\PBS\centering \textbf{ Key lengths (bytes)  }\\\cline{1-4}
\endhead
aes\+\_\+big &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
aes\+\_\+small &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
aes\+\_\+ct &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
aes\+\_\+ct64 &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
aes\+\_\+x86ni &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
aes\+\_\+pwr8 &A\+ES &\PBS\centering 16 &\PBS\centering 16, 24 and 32 \\\cline{1-4}
des\+\_\+ct &D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES &\PBS\centering 8 &\PBS\centering 8, 16 and 24 \\\cline{1-4}
des\+\_\+tab &D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES &\PBS\centering 8 &\PBS\centering 8, 16 and 24 \\\cline{1-4}
\end{longtabu}
{\bfseries Note\+:} D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES nominally uses keys of 64, 128 and 192 bits (i.\+e. 8, 16 and 24 bytes), but some of the bits are ignored by the algorithm, so the {\itshape effective} key lengths, from a security point of view, are 56, 112 and 168 bits, respectively.

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+big} is a \char`\"{}classical\char`\"{} A\+ES implementation, using tables. It is fast but not constant-\/time, since it makes data-\/dependent array accesses.

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+small} is an A\+ES implementation optimized for code size. It is substantially slower than {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+big}; it is not constant-\/time either.

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct} is a constant-\/time implementation of A\+ES; its code is about as big as that of {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+big}, while its performance is comparable to that of {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+small}. However, it is constant-\/time. This implementation should thus be considered to be the \char`\"{}default\char`\"{} A\+ES in Bear\+S\+SL, to be used unless the operational context guarantees that a non-\/constant-\/time implementation is safe, or an architecture-\/specific constant-\/time implementation can be used (e.\+g. using dedicated hardware opcodes).

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct64} is another constant-\/time implementation of A\+ES. It is similar to {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct} but uses 64-\/bit values. On 32-\/bit machines, {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct64} is not faster than {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct}, often a bit slower, and has a larger footprint; however, on 64-\/bit architectures, {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct64} is typically twice faster than {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+ct} for modes that allow parallel operations (i.\+e. C\+TR, and C\+BC decryption, but not C\+BC encryption).

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+x86ni} exists only on x86 architectures (32-\/bit and 64-\/bit). It uses the A\+E\+S-\/\+NI opcodes when available.

{\ttfamily aes\+\_\+pwr8} exists only on Power\+PC / P\+O\+W\+ER architectures (32-\/bit and 64-\/bit, both little-\/endian and big-\/endian). It uses the A\+ES opcodes present in P\+O\+W\+E\+R8 and later.

{\ttfamily des\+\_\+tab} is a classic, table-\/based implementation of D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES. It is not constant-\/time.

{\ttfamily des\+\_\+ct} is an constant-\/time implementation of D\+E\+S/3\+D\+ES. It is substantially slower than {\ttfamily des\+\_\+tab}.

\subsubsection*{Cha\+Cha20 and Poly1305}

Cha\+Cha20 is a stream cipher. Poly1305 is a M\+AC algorithm. They are described in \href{https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7539}{\tt R\+FC 7539}.

Two function pointer types are defined\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run} describes a function that implements Cha\+Cha20 only.
\item {\ttfamily br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run} describes an implementation of Poly1305, in the A\+E\+AD combination with Cha\+Cha20 specified in R\+FC 7539 (the Cha\+Cha20 implementation is provided as a function pointer).
\end{DoxyItemize}

{\ttfamily chacha20\+\_\+ct} is a straightforward implementation of Cha\+Cha20 in plain C; it is constant-\/time, small, and reasonably fast.

{\ttfamily chacha20\+\_\+sse2} leverages S\+S\+E2 opcodes (on x86 architectures that support these opcodes). It is faster than {\ttfamily chacha20\+\_\+ct}.

{\ttfamily poly1305\+\_\+ctmul} is an implementation of the Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 A\+E\+AD construction, where the Poly1305 part is performed with mixed 32-\/bit multiplications (operands are 32-\/bit, result is 64-\/bit).

{\ttfamily poly1305\+\_\+ctmul32} implements Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 using pure 32-\/bit multiplications (32-\/bit operands, 32-\/bit result). It is slower than {\ttfamily poly1305\+\_\+ctmul}, except on some specific architectures such as the A\+RM Cortex M0+.

{\ttfamily poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq} implements Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 with mixed 64-\/bit multiplications (operands are 64-\/bit, result is 128-\/bit) on 64-\/bit platforms that support such operations.

{\ttfamily poly1305\+\_\+i15} implements Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 with the generic \char`\"{}i15\char`\"{} big integer implementation. It is meant mostly for testing purposes, although it can help with saving a few hundred bytes of code footprint on systems where code size is scarce.

\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}}
\index{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}{br\_chacha20\_run}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef uint32\+\_\+t($\ast$ br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run) (const void $\ast$key, const void $\ast$iv, uint32\+\_\+t cc, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len)}



Type for a Cha\+Cha20 implementation. 

An implementation follows the description in R\+FC 7539\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Key is 256 bits ({\ttfamily key} points to exactly 32 bytes).
\item IV is 96 bits ({\ttfamily iv} points to exactly 12 bytes).
\item Block counter is over 32 bits and starts at value {\ttfamily cc}; the resulting value is returned.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Data (pointed to by {\ttfamily data}, of length {\ttfamily len}) is encrypted/decrypted in place. If {\ttfamily len} is not a multiple of 64, then the excess bytes from the last block processing are dropped (therefore, \char`\"{}chunked\char`\"{} processing works only as long as each non-\/final chunk has a length multiple of 64).


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em key} & secret key (32 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em iv} & IV (12 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em cc} & initial counter value. \\
\hline
{\em data} & data to encrypt or decrypt. \\
\hline
{\em len} & data length (in bytes). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{bearssl__block_8h_a657418e5ad2f2667390885239ba0524d}\label{bearssl__block_8h_a657418e5ad2f2667390885239ba0524d}} 
\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run}}
\index{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run}{br\_poly1305\_run}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef void($\ast$ br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run) (const void $\ast$key, const void $\ast$iv, void $\ast$data, size\+\_\+t len, const void $\ast$aad, size\+\_\+t aad\+\_\+len, void $\ast$tag, \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a274de0985f8bb5b252a37526a9591826}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run} ichacha, int encrypt)}



Type for a Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 A\+E\+AD implementation. 

The provided data is encrypted or decrypted with Cha\+Cha20. The authentication tag is computed on the concatenation of the additional data and the ciphertext, with the padding and lengths as described in R\+FC 7539 (section 2.\+8).

After decryption, the caller is responsible for checking that the computed tag matches the expected value.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em key} & secret key (32 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em iv} & nonce (12 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em data} & data to encrypt or decrypt. \\
\hline
{\em len} & data length (in bytes). \\
\hline
{\em aad} & additional authenticated data. \\
\hline
{\em aad\+\_\+len} & length of additional authenticated data (in bytes). \\
\hline
{\em tag} & output buffer for the authentication tag. \\
\hline
{\em ichacha} & implementation of Cha\+Cha20. \\
\hline
{\em encrypt} & non-\/zero for encryption, zero for decryption. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable@{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable}}
\index{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable@{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable()}{br\_aes\_pwr8\_cbcdec\_get\_vtable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a5542970c820eeee2e62766368be8fb7f}{br\+\_\+block\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+class}$\ast$ br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Obtain the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+pwr8} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (decryption) implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to {\ttfamily br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+vtable}, if that implementation was compiled in the library {\itshape and} the P\+O\+W\+E\+R8 crypto opcodes are available on the currently running C\+PU. If either of these conditions is not met, then this function returns {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+pwr8} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (decryption) implementation, or {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable()}{br\_aes\_pwr8\_cbcenc\_get\_vtable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_ad0ecff523e21a74dc1143dcfa52aa251}{br\+\_\+block\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+class}$\ast$ br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Obtain the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+pwr8} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (encryption) implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to {\ttfamily br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+pwr8\+\_\+cbcenc\+\_\+vtable}, if that implementation was compiled in the library {\itshape and} the P\+O\+W\+E\+R8 crypto opcodes are available on the currently running C\+PU. If either of these conditions is not met, then this function returns {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+pwr8} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (encryption) implementation, or {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+x86ni\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable()}{br\_aes\_x86ni\_cbcdec\_get\_vtable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a5542970c820eeee2e62766368be8fb7f}{br\+\_\+block\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+class}$\ast$ br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+x86ni\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+get\+\_\+vtable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Obtain the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+x86ni} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (decryption) implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to {\ttfamily br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+x86ni\+\_\+cbcdec\+\_\+vtable}, if that implementation was compiled in the library {\itshape and} the x86 A\+ES opcodes are available on the currently running C\+PU. If either of these conditions is not met, then this function returns {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+x86ni} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+BC (decryption) implementation, or {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Obtain the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+x86ni} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+TR implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to {\ttfamily br\+\_\+aes\+\_\+x86ni\+\_\+ctr\+\_\+vtable}, if that implementation was compiled in the library {\itshape and} the x86 A\+ES opcodes are available on the currently running C\+PU. If either of these conditions is not met, then this function returns {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}.

the {\ttfamily aes\+\_\+x86ni} A\+E\+S-\/\+C\+TR implementation, or {\ttfamily N\+U\+LL}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+get()}{br\_chacha20\_sse2\_get()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a274de0985f8bb5b252a37526a9591826}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run} br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Obtain the {\ttfamily sse2} Cha\+Cha20 implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to {\ttfamily br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run}, if that implementation was compiled in the library {\itshape and} the S\+S\+E2 opcodes are available on the currently running C\+PU. If either of these conditions is not met, then this function returns {\ttfamily 0}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\ttfamily sse2} Cha\+Cha20 implementation, or {\ttfamily 0}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{bearssl__block_8h_a613995edc096fb28d0493ae98c16cbc0}\label{bearssl__block_8h_a613995edc096fb28d0493ae98c16cbc0}} 
\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run}}
\index{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run()}{br\_chacha20\_sse2\_run()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+run (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const void $\ast$}]{key,  }\item[{const void $\ast$}]{iv,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{cc,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{len }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Cha\+Cha20 implementation (S\+S\+E2 code, constant-\/time). 

This implementation is available only on x86 platforms, depending on compiler support. Moreover, in 32-\/bit mode, it might not actually run, if the underlying hardware does not implement the S\+S\+E2 opcode (in 64-\/bit mode, S\+S\+E2 is part of the A\+BI, so if the code could be compiled at all, then it can run). Use {\ttfamily \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_aec92d1ee7450cf0859a9c8a949764376}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+sse2\+\_\+get()}} to safely obtain a pointer to that function.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a274de0985f8bb5b252a37526a9591826}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em key} & secret key (32 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em iv} & IV (12 bytes). \\
\hline
{\em cc} & initial counter value. \\
\hline
{\em data} & data to encrypt or decrypt. \\
\hline
{\em len} & data length (in bytes). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+get()}{br\_poly1305\_ctmulq\_get()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a657418e5ad2f2667390885239ba0524d}{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run} br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void}]{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Get the Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 \char`\"{}ctmulq\char`\"{} implementation, if available. 

This function returns a pointer to the {\ttfamily \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a7e37eb1c81fd560222c9aed6e617159d}{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run()}} function if supported on the current platform; otherwise, it returns 0.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the ctmulq Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 implementation, or 0. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{bearssl__block_8h_a7e37eb1c81fd560222c9aed6e617159d}\label{bearssl__block_8h_a7e37eb1c81fd560222c9aed6e617159d}} 
\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run}}
\index{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run()}{br\_poly1305\_ctmulq\_run()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+run (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const void $\ast$}]{key,  }\item[{const void $\ast$}]{iv,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{len,  }\item[{const void $\ast$}]{aad,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{aad\+\_\+len,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{tag,  }\item[{\hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a274de0985f8bb5b252a37526a9591826}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}}]{ichacha,  }\item[{int}]{encrypt }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 A\+E\+AD implementation (ctmulq). 

This implementation uses 64-\/bit multiplications (result over 128 bits). It is available only on platforms that offer such a primitive (in practice, 64-\/bit architectures). Use {\ttfamily \hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a0c2b86940f73e4db3894709494080b97}{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+ctmulq\+\_\+get()}} to dynamically obtain a pointer to that function, or 0 if not supported.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}!br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run}}
\index{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run@{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run}!bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h@{bearssl\+\_\+block.\+h}}
\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run()}{br\_poly1305\_i15\_run()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+i15\+\_\+run (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const void $\ast$}]{key,  }\item[{const void $\ast$}]{iv,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{len,  }\item[{const void $\ast$}]{aad,  }\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{aad\+\_\+len,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{tag,  }\item[{\hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a274de0985f8bb5b252a37526a9591826}{br\+\_\+chacha20\+\_\+run}}]{ichacha,  }\item[{int}]{encrypt }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Cha\+Cha20+\+Poly1305 A\+E\+AD implementation (i15). 

This implementation relies on the generic big integer code \char`\"{}i15\char`\"{} (which uses pure 32-\/bit multiplications). As such, it may save a little code footprint in a context where \char`\"{}i15\char`\"{} is already included (e.\+g. for elliptic curves or for R\+SA); however, it is also substantially slower than the ctmul and ctmul32 implementations.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\hyperlink{bearssl__block_8h_a657418e5ad2f2667390885239ba0524d}{br\+\_\+poly1305\+\_\+run}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
